Each collection will have ten volumes, totaling one hundred volumes, using new materials and adopting the old chapter-style literary form like the Kaiyuan Stories, to make it enjoyable for readers. Hence, it is named the Story Series. All collections will be published within the year, and continuous compilation will continue thereafter, it is said.

Little Boy (68)

— Original by American author Louisa May Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"I don't care where I go or how long I stay, but I'll be damned if I come back," Don said with a burst of anger, then went to pack his things, all of which had originally been given to him by Mr.裴.

This was also his farewell speech to the children, because they were discussing the matter in the barn when he came down. He didn't want Ned to call them. A carriage stopped at the door, and Mrs. Pei went out to speak to Don. The sadness on her face broke his heart, so he gently asked:

"May I see Tommy one more time?"

"Of course; go in and kiss him. He'll be very sad not to see his Don."

He bent over the cradle, and the little face lit up as soon as it saw him. No one saw the anxious look in Don's own eyes. At the same time, he heard Mrs. Pei pleading:

"Can't we give this poor child another chance, Mr. Pei?" Mr. Pei then replied in his decisive tone:

"My dear, this isn't the best way. Let him stay somewhere harmless and beneficial to himself for a while, and he'll be back soon, you'll see."

Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Ji Ren)

"Only women and petty people are difficult to nurture. If you get close to them, they become disrespectful; if you keep them at a distance, they resent you." As someone with limited experience of the world, I didn't fully understand the weight of these "sage words" at first. However, in recent years, I've traveled around and had more opportunities to interact with society. I've come to believe that Confucius's remarks, though separated by thousands of years, remain unchanged. Indeed, they are a "definitive statement." I ask you: Aren't the actions of women and petty people something that cannot be completely eradicated from society? Would society cease to be society without such people? I dare to ask those who are wise.

"People who are helped don't leave, but ghosts run straight away." These are two common sayings. One must be careful in choosing friends. People with responsibility and those unwilling to fall behind should have a kind of "knowing people" and "knowing talent" wisdom. Insight is essential.

"Treading on thin ice" is the style of a humble gentleman. Nowadays, once people achieve success, they often have a sense of "I am the only one worthy" and "who but me." One should know that a tall tree catches the wind. If there's a mistake one day, you'll realize that the sails were set too high, and the danger is even greater than anything else.

Those born into poverty often achieve great success and become great figures.

Friends who are accustomed to "stealing chickens and cutting threads" will start to suspect that others are also learning their "stealing chickens and cutting threads" ways once they gain power. Therefore, they constantly guard against others, fearing that it's not thorough enough. However, everyone has their own "character" and their own "background." Wasting effort is futile and only invites boredom. Why bother?

General Mobilization Order

— Qing Qu

Hearing the word "mobilization" makes my heart leap, because it's like a torch burning forward on the front lines of war. No matter how solemn the League of Nations in Geneva, a peace organization, it's immediately shattered, and many alliances are destroyed in an instant. Alas! Moreover, the word "total" and "order" are added above and below "mobilization." This shows that the entire nation is united in attacking the enemy, and no one can escape this order. So, what's frightening is "mobilization," and what's most terrifying is "general mobilization order."

You! It's heard that both sides have issued a "general mobilization order," and everyone is preparing to attack East Africa? This war, compared to the First European War twenty years ago, has many more advanced weapons. Now, they're all going to be used to turn Abyssinia into a battlefield and test them out first. Although it's impossible to predict which country will win and which will lose, the old saying "war is fierce and dangerous" is something that no one can deny. Moreover, it's said that everything in terms of military equipment is just a facade. Once those scientifically secret inventions are unleashed in the midst of a desperate battle between the two armies, humph! A death ray will be released, and no matter how strong the city or defensive structure, it will immediately become ineffective. Even a group of fighter planes in the sky, like flying mosquitoes, will turn into nothing. You! Don't you think this kind of war is a great disaster for the world and humanity?

Alas, peace! peace! After shouting for many years, it's given up with a "general mobilization order." So, any country that constantly adopts an attitude of appeasement, fearing to fight with the enemy, is always suffering from cowardice. However, if someone likes to start trouble, willingly becoming the leader of the war, and believes that they are invincible, then this is not really a righteous war with a "just cause." You! Look at Napoleon, who held the Bible in his left hand and the sword in his right. Although he won repeatedly and dominated the world, alas! In the end, he was imprisoned on the island of Saint Helena. I ask you, where did he actually gain victory?

Miss Sausage

— Hua Ling

This column once published an article about "Miss Chocolate." Unexpectedly, things in the world are never unique. Near a certain university, there is a "Miss Sausage," which translated means "Sausage Lady."

Near that university, there are a total of three small Western restaurants. Miss Sausage is the wife of the owner of one of these three small Western restaurants. Although this small Western restaurant, like the other two, has a name and an enamel sign, the university students always say when they go to this Western restaurant, "Let's go to Miss Sausage's place."

Miss Sausage is the owner's second wife, only twenty-one or two years old. She is neither tall nor short, neither fat nor thin. She has a dimple on her left cheek and a gray mole the size of a bedbug on her right cheek. So, the university students all admit that her dimple is like that of a certain star, and her gray mole is like that of a certain star.

She treats customers very attentively, making them feel as comfortable as they are at home. She can say the English names of various dishes, especially the word "sausage," which she pronounces fluently, so she became "Miss Sausage."

Each meal, there are about a hundred customers under Miss Sausage's hospitality. Because Miss Sausage's hospitality is attentive, the small tips are given a lot. So Miss Sausage always has her hair permed, wears high heels, and is very modern.

Among the three Western restaurants, Miss Sausage's is the smallest, but six or seven out of ten of the diners in that university are her customers. The other two "lower prices," "offer credit," and "also use female waitresses," but Miss Sausage's business is not affected at all.

Recently, around three or four o'clock in the afternoon, the university students have been popularizing a slogan, "Let's go to Miss Sausage's place for milk coffee!"

Chapter 20: Struggling to See the Beloved Grandson, Crying Together, Recalling the Past in a Year of Famine, Sowing Wheat to Invite Disaster

Shi Lian scratched his head and said with a smile, "I have something very difficult. Just now I went to this back door and saw an old woman sitting under the opposite door frame, about to die. I thought, that must be Mr. Jia's new wife's grandmother. When I saw it, I naturally had to tell them." The tea attendant laughed, "Then why don't you tell them?" Li Shi Lian said, "I'm afraid that the new wife will feel bad when she hears it." The tea attendant laughed, "If she feels bad, let Mr. Jia feel sorry for her, what are you worried about, Mr. Li?" The tea attendant said, walking forward, Li Shi Lian grabbed him and asked, "In your Xi'an city, are there any people who borrow illness to extort money?" The tea attendant said, "Where did you hear that? I haven't heard of it." He didn't answer completely, and he was already far away. Shi Lian thought, "That's bad, he's already gone to the front, he must have told her everything." Maybe old Jia himself will come to the back to take a look. Even if the old woman of the Zhu family is trying to extort money from me by dying, I'm not afraid of him with her grandson-in-law present. Moreover, the tea attendant said that there is no such thing in Xi'an city. Thinking this way, it seems that it is still better to go to the back door to take a look. Fortunately, there is still a street separating us from the opposite door. Even if she wants to extort money from me, she can't." Thinking this way, he turned around and went to the back door again. From afar, he saw Yue Ying's mother and that Hu sister-in-law, all sitting on the door frame. The old woman was leaning against her daughter-in-law, still slightly opening her eyes, she was definitely not dead. His daughter-in-law and Hu sister-in-law were holding a bowl of water, giving her a drink. (334)

The Misty Records of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Especially our Empress Dowager, she is usually very careful to decorate her appearance, and she changes her clothes very diligently. I think she will definitely not be willing to let her body be the only place to hide dirt and filth. But at first, I couldn't guess how her bathing problem was solved.

Now let me first say how I solved it myself? Fortunately, the Empress Dowager treated us specially. Although the first few female officials who entered all lived together in a side hall behind the Empress Dowager's bedroom, six people lived together, for the convenience of the Empress Dowager's calling. But when we entered, the Empress Dowager knew that we would never want to live so crowded. Therefore, not only did she specially designate two small houses for us in the palace, but also in the Summer Palace, we also had separate residences. With this convenience, we can buy our own bathing equipment, but it can't be very complete. I just sent a eunuch to my home to send a letter. In less than five or six days, my father entrusted someone to bring us a wooden tub that looked a bit like a Western-style bathtub, and the wood used was very light, so it was not difficult to move. This solved the bathing problem for us sisters.

Next, let me tell you about the Empress Dowager's bathing method.

A few days later, one night, a female official suddenly came to inform me and say: tonight the Empress Dowager is going to take a bath again. Later I finally knew that the Empress Dowager was not only not someone who never bathed all year round, but also had to take a bath every few days, just like she had to apply egg white and camellia dew every night, which was the same unchangeable routine. —Today it is my turn to be on duty, so I must hurry up to serve. (431)

Miscellaneous Talk

From the Town God Temple to the Inner Garden

— Huo Yunming

Everyone who has lived in Shanghai for a long time knows the Town God Temple in Xiaodongdou. Everyone who knows the Town God Temple also knows the Yu Garden behind the temple. Those who grew up nearby, who go to the Huxin Pavilion or Chunfeng Deyi Building for tea at dawn, and meet acquaintances on the road, will ask, "Where are you going?" His answer is: "Going to drink tea in the garden!" Replacing "Yu Garden" with the two words "in the garden" has almost become a common and well-known name.

Upper-class Chinese people have their own Yiyuan dog racing track, Jai Alai court, and dance halls with crystal floors. Shouldn't ordinary people be allowed to sneak into the Town God Temple to find weak entertainment? The brass ring emits a crystal light, which looks no different from real gold. Sipping a bowl of rich, glutinous rice balls, the taste is not inferior to international royal meals and Sullivan's; leaning on the red granite of the Nine-Bend Corridor, leisurely admiring the turtles in the thick green ripples, the style is no less elegant than gazing and pondering on the high floor of the Cathay Hotel. But isn't there also bitter tears in here? Moreover, in the magnificent temple supported by steel and cement, there are statues of the Ming Dynasty dressed with official garments and hats, worshiped by women who are scented with Parisian perfume and young men in stylish suits; isn't this a reflection of national education? However, people criticize the Town God Temple, thinking that it is a recreational area for the masses, gathering a dissolute group every day! They never think that in the Town God Temple, in addition to smoking opium, idle eating, worshiping, and wandering around, there are also schools, hospitals, libraries, public security bureaus, and administrative organs managing the Town God Temple and Yu Garden! People only see the bad side, only curse the back of the mirror for not shining, but they are unwilling to run to the front and take a look at the true essence of the Town God Temple. Just looking at how the roads and sanitation facilities are, is too unfair! What's more, the Lingtai Inner Garden has already been opened, and following the Cui Xiu Hall, famous for its large rockery, it is said that it will also be open to the public on the ninth day of the lunar month.

Here, let me first talk about the story of the Inner Garden and others. Because recently I saw articles describing the Inner Garden, often lumping it together with the large rockery of Cui Xiu Hall. How can they not know that Cui Xiu Hall is called "West Garden," while the Inner Garden is called "East Garden"? According to research, Yu Garden was originally the private residence of Pan Yunduan, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Punishment. The Shanghai County Chronicle says that the garden base has a total of thirty-six acres, eight fen, nine li, and one hao. However, Qiao Zhongwu's record says, "The site is about seventeen acres, south to the temple shrine, the northwest sides are surrounded by walls; the east is Tonghe; a garden gate is opened in the middle..." But from today's point of view, even if the old school grounds west of Small World, the Five Old Peaks to the north (inside Xinbeimen Street), and Anren Street to the east are included, it is definitely not as large as seventeen acres of land, let alone thirty acres, several fen, and several li. After Yu Garden was destroyed, some local people still built gardens on its original site, east of the temple shrine, which was called the "East Garden," constructed in the forty-eighth year of Kangxi, and also known as the "Inner Garden." It used to be managed by the money shop industry. The "West Garden" of the large rockery was built in the twenty-fifth year of Qianlong. In the Inner Garden, the ponds and rockeries are arranged very exquisitely. The rockeries are also more delicate than those in Cui Xiu Hall. Walking up to the left from the small pavilion of "Another World," and finishing the winding stone steps, there is a pavilion, located on a brick hill, where you can have tea or play chess. If you have the interest to "go up another level," you can rely on it to look down on the houses of thousands of families in the city. Exiting the pavilion and going south, there is a row of vermilion painted long houses, comfortable and quiet. During the Republic of China, the Shanghai Municipal Annals Museum used to work there. Originally, from these houses, you could reach the "Small Lingtai" in the southwest corner, but now it is closed, probably used by the gardener as a bedroom? I remember Cao Yishi had a poem: "Red atmosphere and black shadows have been there for years, relying on climbing the terrace to sweep them away." Looking at the bandits in Western Sichuan and the remnant borders in the Northeast, there is no place to mourn, it is really pitiful.

The Inner Garden's encircling walls are all engraved with mud dragons. The dragon's heads are directly immersed in the pool water. It is said that the dragon has nine heads, but only six or seven can be found. In fact, it is a nonsense rumor. The most elegant place in the garden is in a concave corridor on the east side of the main hall, which happens to embrace the pool. A cluster of green bamboo grows out of the reef pile. If you can sit there in the drizzling rain at dusk and listen to the whisper of late autumn, you will definitely understand the beauty of the Inner Garden and the stillness of the Inner Garden.

Page 13

Economic Supplement

The Path to Improving China's Economy

— Yu Huancheng

Liu An: This article is a lecture manuscript by Mr. Huancheng at Fudan University and Great China University. There are varying opinions on the path to improving China's economy. Mr. Huancheng presents his thoughts of over ten years, expressing them in this article, advocating for integrating industry into agriculture. This is undoubtedly extraordinary, and scholars at home and abroad will surely gain a new interest in research from this article. However, due to the limited space in this publication, the full text is over ten thousand words, which cannot be completed in one issue. The remainder will be published in installments.

I. Reflections of Recent Years

What I am talking about today is what methods should be used to improve China's economy? I dare not say transform, only improve, because transformation requires a complete overhaul to be worthy of the word "transform," while improvement implies partial and temporary progress; however, it also requires the word "change."

Although it is called improvement, it seems more stable and accommodating. However, this issue is still very important and complex. What I am talking about today is naturally not a doctrine, nor a system; but rather a reflection that has arisen from what I have seen and heard in recent years. I have held this reflection for almost ten years, but it has not yet formed a system, nor have I collected various materials, so I have not written this reflection into an article, nor have I spoken about it in detail to anyone. Now, China's economic situation is deteriorating day by day, almost reaching a dead end. From top to bottom, the call for economic transformation is growing louder day by day, creating the impression that it is impossible to move forward without change. In this trend, I naturally cannot help but want to reveal my reflections of the past ten years for my fellow students to study together.

Where did my reflections originate? About eleven or twelve years ago, I went to see the Daye Iron Mine. There were hundreds of workers digging ore sand. I asked the manager, "Where do the workers come from?" The manager replied, "These are all farmers from nearby areas. There are fewer workers during the busy farming season, and more during the slack season. The nearby villages benefit a lot from the iron mine." I realized that mining was originally a kind of sideline for farmers. Why are there no workers to recruit other than farmers? Why do farmers not have other better sidelines than mining? Why do they still do farm work during the busy season, instead of making mining a profession? This was the first time I had a doubtful reflection.

About five or six years ago, I had a friend named Wang, who had been dealing in flour mill machinery since flour mills started being established in China. He told me, "This time I came back from Shandong, and the small flour mills in Shandong are developing tremendously. Since the advent of diesel engines, a small flour mill can be set up with a few thousand or ten thousand yuan. The local wheat is milled into flour locally, making buying and selling convenient and saving transportation costs, so they can often earn a bit. There are many machine flour mills in the villages." At that time, I realized that flour mills could be set up in the villages, so why couldn't other factories be set up in the villages? Village flour milling can switch to small machines, so why can't other agricultural sidelines and village handicrafts be mechanized? This was the second time I had the reflection of combining agriculture and industry, and village factories.

Recently, three or four years ago, my friend Gao Jiansi invited me to visit the People's Education Institute in Wuxi. Seeing its achievements in improving rural areas, training citizens, literacy education, and cooperative sales, I also realized that farmers are not stubborn and foolish. As long as someone promotes and trains them, they will make progress by leaps and bounds. Unfortunately, I didn't have the time to visit Ding County, Zouping, Nanzhao, and other places that are improving rural areas, so I could have gained more insights. This was the third time I had the reflection that farmers can accomplish great things.

Combining these reflections and casually consulting some newspapers and books, I felt that China's economy has its own stance. To improve China's economy, there is a clear and open path. I thought, questioned, and answered myself. In the past two or three years, I have almost had a draft of a concrete plan in my mind, which is what I am going to talk about today. In reality, it is still just a reflection. However, I have combined my previous reflections and tentatively proposed some ideas.

Now we must enter the main text. If we want to improve China's economy, we must first understand what kind of object China's economy is. For example, a doctor treating a disease must first recognize what the disease is, and what the patient's physical condition is, before prescribing medicine. It is not copying a universal panacea that can be applied casually, nor is it that the old and young, men and women, strong and weak, can all be treated with the same prescription. Speaking of prescriptions for treating China's economy, there are really too many! Free trade, protectionist policies, agriculturalism, industrialization, up to the most modern controlled economy, planned economy, all can be said to be reasonable. Talking about imitating other countries! England completed its industrial development through free trade, Germany achieved industrial revitalization through protective tariffs; the countries of the Americas have achieved national prosperity by using foreign capital. There have already been many precedents in history. Recently, such as Soviet Russia's Five-Year Plan, Italy's corporatist system, and even Denmark's rural cooperation, and England's Guild socialism, have been praised by many people, and advocated by many people. Which one is good in the end? It is confusing, and there is a sense of being lost and not knowing where to go. I think various theories and systems of various countries are all good, and they are all not good. Good or not, depends on whether it suits the object of our country. If it suits, it is good, if it doesn't suit, it is not good. If there is no theory or system that can be completely and perfectly applied like a printed plate, we must also deliberate on what to take and what to discard, combine various methods, or come up with new ideas to handle it. The so-called "the miracle of application lies in the mind," it is not tracing every detail and copying imitations that can be done well and handled properly.

Speaking of the object of our country's economy, the talk becomes complicated. Marxist scholars are arguing about what period and what stage? Feudal! Pre-capitalist! Capitalist! They have been arguing for a long time, and they still can't figure it out clearly. I am an outsider, and I am even more confused. Now, let's not use these general and all-encompassing names for the time being, and just list a few special phenomena in fact, which may be easier to understand. Let's just talk about the facts.

II. The Economy of the Family System or Patriarchal Society

The most obvious fact is that the vast majority of our country, or even the entire country, is the economy of the family system; it can also be said to be the economy of the patriarchal society. In most villages, people live in clans, such as a certain family village or a certain family manor, which is everywhere. Even in Shanghai, there are still traces of Tangjiazhai and Gujialong. Among those who live together, prosperous families have ancestral halls, and ancestral halls have clan rules. The most important is ancestor worship, followed by helping clansmen; there are clan estates, clan schools, and public property of the clan awarded to those who have achieved honor. The family is the center of life for Chinese people. In terms of family ethics, the family is important, and the individual is light. In terms of family concepts, one only knows the family, and does not know the country. According to modern new theories, this is the poison of feudalism. However, the vast majority of people in the country, especially farmers, are immersed in the river of family love, deeply rooted and difficult to eradicate. Despite the shouts of overthrowing the old ethics and breaking the old morality in several major cities; and several rounds of people bravely attacking the Confucius shop, attacking once, twice, three times, attacking endlessly; in fact, there are also fathers and sons, mothers and daughters, suing each other, and it seems that family ethics and family concepts have been shaken by the new trend. However, this is only the current situation in a few major cities; if we compare the population of these major cities with the national population, we will feel that the shaking power of the new trend is not enough to even scratch the surface. The population table of each city is listed below: (According to the Twenty-Fourth Year of the Shen Bao Almanac)

Nanjing City 726,131 Hangzhou City 550,990

Shanghai City 3,480,018 Qingdao City 451,184

Beiping City 1,516,378 Chengdu City 440,859

Guangzhou City 1,222,583 Chongqing City 281,271

Tianjin City 1,399,146 Shantou City 208,608

Hankou City 772,834 Wuhu City 150,411

Changsha City 408,005

The above thirteen urban areas, including the suburban population, are still less than 12 million people. Adding the more industrialized and commercial areas in the south such as Xiamen, Fuzhou, and the central region such as Ningbo, Wuxi, Suzhou, Yangzhou, and the northern region such as Jinan, Taiyuan, Zhangjiakou, Baotou, etc., about 3.4 million people, the total is no more than 15.6 million. According to the national population of over 430 million, it is still less than 4 percent. The number is already too small, not to mention that in these more industrialized and commercial cities, there are only a very small number of new intellectuals, and unrestrained young men and women, who jump out of the family circle and act on their own. On the other hand, 80 or 90 percent still live family lives, keeping family customs; although they live in cities, they have not been affected by individualism, nationalism, or socialism. It can be said that the entire country is within the scope of the family. Therefore, the economy cannot be separated from the economy of the family system.

What are the economic phenomena of the family system? Mr. Qianxi explained it very clearly in "China's New Economic Policy." I quote it as follows: "Europeans and Americans value the concept of the state, and undervalue the concept of the family; Chinese individuals value the concept of the family, and undervalue the concept of the state. The scope of the family also varies in size. In Europe and America, the rights and obligations of individual property related to the family are mostly limited to spouses; in China, the rights and obligations of individual property related to the family, direct relatives, collateral relatives, and even relatives and friends, all have a legal, customary, and moral relationship of property rights and obligations. (Omission) The status of Europeans and Americans in society is very different from the status of Chinese people in society. Europeans and Americans are responsible to the state and individuals in society; Chinese people are responsible to the state and individuals in society, and must also bear a broad family responsibility. In summary, the spirit of the European and American social structure is to make all members powerful, and to minimize the scope of the powerless members; the spirit of the Chinese social structure is to make all members, both powerful and powerless, coexist, and to preserve the habit of powerless members relying on the existence of powerful members. Therefore, whether they are employed or unemployed, property owners or propertyless, their economic environments are absolutely different in Europe and America and in China. (Omission) European and American laws and customs are mainly focused on wealth accumulation; Chinese laws and customs are mainly focused on wealth equalization." This passage reveals the economic reality of China's thousands of years of tradition, truly seeing the big picture and revealing the minute details. Compared to those who use the two words "overthrow" and "establish" to obliterate everything, it is not the same. The effect of the family system economy is entirely focused on compassion and harmony (see the Rites of Zhou). Frankly speaking, it is that people with money have to bear the responsibility of helping poor relatives. Mr. Qianxi therefore said that wealth equalization is the main focus. However, although it is wealth equalization, it only equalizes to people with blood ties, and not to the entire society; "love relatives and be benevolent to the people, be benevolent to the people and love things," (see Mencius,) there is a difference.

The advantages of the family system economy are: (1) Reducing the difference between the rich and the poor. (2) Making people love their clans and hometowns. (3) Making customs simple and honest, the so-called "carefully pursuing the distant ancestors, and the people's morality will return to honesty," (see the Analects.) The disadvantages are that it is incompatible with various new trends, especially capitalism. Because capitalism focuses on the development of individual abilities, and requires considerable abilities to do considerable things. The family system both restricts individuals and makes their property easy to disperse, and when doing things and employing people, relatives and fellow villagers are entangled and unclear, often making those who do things procrastinate and reduce efficiency. A certain industrial magnate has a very large business, but the personnel he employs are either relatives or clansmen. In the office, the conversation is all in the same local accent, and the result is inevitably failure. This is not because the abilities of a certain magnate are insufficient, but because it is putting new wine in old bottles. The family system is incompatible with capitalism. For decades, capitalist-style new industries have been promoted in major commercial ports, but the result has not created new capital, but has lost more old capital. Naturally, there are other important reasons, and the family system is certainly a spreader of plague for capitalism.

Since the family system contains the meaning of wealth equalization, "the wealthy are not benevolent, and the benevolent are not wealthy!" (see Mencius) "Alas for the rich! Pity the poor and lonely," (see the Book of Songs) wealth has always been a moral concept in the family system that is not very much admired. Therefore, socialism is easier to approach than capitalism. However, collective socialism is also feared to be incompatible. I think that warm, reformed, socialism, using cooperative methods, can combine and dissolve material civilization into the family system. Paying attention to both production and distribution at the same time may be more possible. Or it can achieve a path of less effort and more success, less sacrifice and greater efficiency.

III. The Historical Nature of Emphasis on Agriculture and the Phenomenon of the Suffering of Farmers Who Account for the Largest Proportion of the National Population

"Agriculture is the fundamental wealth, and industry and commerce are the secondary wealth." This is the traditional economic thought of China for thousands of years since the Zhou and Qin dynasties. From Hou Ji, Duke Zhou, Guan Zhong, Shang Yang, Jia Yi, Chao Cuo, all the way to Gu Tinglin and Zhang Yangyuan of the former Qing Dynasty, it has been passed down without any changes. Those who hold different opinions are only the smallest minority (such as Huang Lizhou's saying that "all are fundamental"), and have no influence on society. Emperors and local officials often personally plowed the land during the Spring Festival, and the ceremony was extremely grand (much more grand than planting trees on Arbor Day now). When we were young, we often heard the saying "passing down the family through farming and reading." Farming and reading were both noble occupations. Until modern times, returning to the fields is still a fashionable phrase on the lips of generals and bureaucrats. In addition to untitled poems (romantic love) and social poems, most of Chinese literature is pastoral literature, either elaborating on the hardships of farmers or singing the joys of rural life. In general, the psychology of the past has been that, in terms of a country, agriculture is the fundamental wealth of the country; in terms of individuals, agriculture is the most noble life. The concept of emphasizing agriculture has not been changed or abandoned from history to today. However, on the one hand, despite the emphasis on agriculture, there are many elegant and beautiful texts; on the other hand, the farmers are extremely poor. At best, they can only live a stable minimum life. Mencius said, "In good years, they suffer all their lives, and in bad years, they cannot avoid death." Until we see it, it is still the case. It cannot be said that this is a very contradictory phenomenon. In recent years, soldiers and bandits have risen one after another, and floods and droughts have occurred intermittently. You often see in newspapers the facts of eating grass roots, swallowing tree bark, digging Guanyin powder, refugees fleeing famine, families committing suicide or starving to death. These are all the circumstances of the largest number of farmers in a country that claims to value agriculture, struggling to live in an environment where they cannot live. Speaking of it, it is really tragic! It is really painful! The farmers, who account for 82-83 percent of the national population, are mired in such a miserable situation, even if a dozen or so major cities are created as golden paradises and fairy lands, how much can they do to remedy the national economy? Can a small number of industries and businesses still prosper if the majority of farmers are so miserable? Who will consume the manufactured goods and who will buy the goods transported by merchants? Talking about the improvement of China's economy, without thinking about the largest number of most miserable farmers, is always "putting the cart before the horse," and there is no good in it.

IV. The Status of a Semi-Colony and the Complex Phenomenon of the New and the Old

Advanced countries have many ways to improve their economies. However, they mostly acquire the land of others to supply their colonies. In our country, others colonize our own land. This crucial point is just the opposite. The economies of colonized and colonized countries are fundamentally different. Can we use the entire protectionist policy of Germany? Can we, like England, ostensibly claim free trade, but secretly exploit colonies to enrich ourselves? Can we do what the countries of the Americas do, freely absorbing foreign capital to increase production? Can we follow the example of the majority of modern countries, even the smallest free cities, in managing exchange rates and distributing imports? This cannot be done, and that cannot be done. Commercial treaties and concessions bind us so that we cannot move. In addition to unequal treaties, there are also unilateral agreements imposed by powerful neighbors; in addition to concessions, there are also forced demilitarized zones. Others compete to build tariff barriers, but we insist on reducing taxes; others compete to protect their factories, but we make factories run by others better than our own factories. Originally, the status of a semi-colony is quickly rising to a full colony. Many things outside of the economy make it impossible to start improving the economy. If imperialism cannot be defeated politically, the economy can only bow its head and listen to its aggression. When the mountains and rivers are exhausted, where can we find a way out?

The semi-colonial status has already made the economy have no way to go. There is another difficulty: our country is in a transitional period, and things from thousands of years ago are mixed with modern things. Airplanes are flying in the sky, and on the ground, carters are driving their carts with a pair of horses, just like when Confucius traveled around the states, one cart and two horses, it is still the same. Conflicting and uncoordinated phenomena are everywhere in society. When various countries first changed to machines, a certain number of unemployed people naturally occurred. Fortunately, they have colonies and uncivilized people to develop sales channels; therefore, emerging industries are rising vigorously. Not only is it easy for the unemployed to find jobs, but their lives are also particularly prosperous, and conflicts will naturally not last long. Our country is too backward. The light industry that once developed cannot resist foreign goods, but it is more than enough to defeat local goods. In the end, it was defeated by foreign forces and will perish together with local goods. We see that factories in cities support thousands and tens of thousands of workers, but we don't know how many thousands and tens of thousands of people are unemployed and even lose their food in the interior. To give a simple example. "Men plow and women weave" is the custom of China's family economy and rural economy that has been passed down for thousands of years. In the past, almost every family in the countryside had a Gandhi-style spinning machine. The weaving technology was better, and the places where cloth was produced were famous, and every family had a loom. Since the development of machine textile factories, they first eliminated hand-spinning machines in the countryside, and then eliminated weaving machines in cloth-producing areas. There is only men plowing, and no more women weaving. Rural women have no work to do. The countryside lacks a major sideline industry. I am not surprised; I am not surprised that machine textiles eliminate Gandhi-style spinning machines. Because even if machine textiles are not run domestically, foreign yarn and cloth will come in torrents and will still eliminate local spinning and weaving. What I am most surprised by is that machine textiles have eliminated local spinning and weaving for many years, and no one has ever thought of another job for rural women to replace spinning and weaving. I see the struggle between domestic goods and local goods (see the Chinese Youth Weekly last year) and I really feel at a loss. How can new industries and old unemployment be taken care of at the same time? If you say that old unemployment can be ignored! Then the unemployed will be unemployed forever, because new industries cannot accommodate so many people. Moreover, such a fragile and pitiful new industry, with capital, machinery, technology, management, and operation that are not as good as others, cannot be protected by the government, and has no united industry association below. Competing with advanced industrialized countries is always uncertain, so how can they take care of old unemployment? The unemployed, in addition to relying on family assistance, have only two ways out: starving to death or committing suicide! To find a third way out, it is inevitable to cause social unrest. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, only the dismissal of postmen caused the chaos of the rebel Li Zicheng. What about adding ten or a hundred times the number of postmen? Those who read foreign books to death and are enthusiastic about industrialization always say that the rise of new industries is inevitable to avoid old unemployment; in this period of new and old transition, it can be ignored, I really have nothing to say to such people, I can only ask them to fast for a few days, to taste the taste of hunger, so that they know how difficult it is to be hungry, and understand whether people who are unemployed and lose their food will wholeheartedly want to cause trouble. "Fools are afraid of the sky falling, and the poor hope to rebel." Who dares to say that there will definitely be no chaos of rebel Li Zicheng in this world? When the new and the old are mixed, this side must be taken care of, and that side must also be taken care of. Agricultural policies! Industrialization! Not only is copying the articles of other countries irrelevant; but even our country's inherent methods of governance cannot be fully applied! Because of such a binding, the semi-colonial status, and the complex phenomenon of the new and old coexisting, is something that no other country has, and has not been seen in our country since ancient times.

V. Several Impossible Paths

I said above that the good and bad of various theories and systems of various countries depend on whether they suit the object of our country. In other words, there is no need to ask whether it is good or bad, just see if it is possible. If it is impossible, no matter how much effort we put in, we will still end up with nothing. Procrastinating again and again, the so-called restoration and the so-called revolution have been going on for decades, and we still cannot find a way out economically. "Time, time, does not wait for people!" We cannot afford to take impossible paths again. Futile efforts should be a lesson to us.

First, the impossibility of capitalism: I said above that the family system is incompatible with capitalism, which is still latent. The development of capitalism has two elements: one is considerable national strength, which can maintain internal peace and resist external aggression (both in terms of military and economy); the other is colonies and uncivilized areas for supply and extraction, which can obtain cheap raw materials and expand the sales channels for finished products. What is our national strength? Where are our colonies and areas for us to extract? Wanting to cross without a boat, wanting to fish without a line, I don't know how to embark on the path of capitalism? Wanting to be a certain magnate will only end up like the Swedish match magnate.

Second, the impossibility of state capitalism: Concentrating capital in the state, with all industries run by the state, and production and consumption also controlled by the state; to achieve this, the most important thing is absolute centralization of power, and the second is extremely good administrative efficiency. These two are what we lack. Even if we have these two conditions, the concessions are horizontal and vertical, and everything has a supreme force there to manipulate. Before capital can be concentrated in the state, it has already fled, so how can we start?

Third, the impossibility of corporatism: Italy's corporatist organization is indeed! In the middle of capitalist state capitalism, another kind of controlled situation is created. However, this also requires considerable national strength and appropriate talents. Our national strength is out of the question; the leading talents cannot be found either. In the past, the result of boycotting certain goods and campaigning for certain things was that a few people filled their pockets. The so-called certain associations are all disguised versions of local tyrants and evil gentry who are manipulating them. Everyone is frowning and suffering the pain of the bamboo pole, with no effect of control at all. Fortunately, China does not have an Italian fascist emperor who is so strong and powerful, otherwise, the people would be even more unbearable to bear this "bamboo pole tribute."

I said above: "The family system inherently contains the meaning of wealth equalization, so socialism is easier to approach than capitalism. I want to use cooperative methods to combine and dissolve material civilization into the family system." Now the government is not promoting cooperation! Unfortunately, they have not recognized the object of China's economy, they are "baffled", and the financial system has not been improved, they cannot get working capital, and the administrative efficiency is too poor, so it has not been very effective. (To be continued)

Securities - The Bond Market Environment is Quite Adverse

The securities market last week (September 30 to October 5) was completely surrounded by the environment. Internal and external troubles came one after another. The Italy-Abyssinia War had begun, and rumors were rampant domestically, making it impossible to investigate. Short selling was naturally crowded, and most long positions were disheartened. Only investment in spot goods was not shaken, so although market prices fluctuated greatly, they did not collapse. Last week's experience was quite repetitive. Generally, No. 48 was sold off for several days and bought back on Friday and Saturday. No. 11 and No. 16 were sold off throughout the week, and the rest mostly sold more and bought less, showing a tendency to adapt to the circumstances. No. 4 and No. 43 also gradually leaned towards selling. Although the market downturn was severe, the rebound was also rapid. Retail investors were sometimes long and sometimes short, in a state of disarray. Monday's rumors triggered selling by the northern gangs, causing prices to fall by several jiao to about one yuan. On Tuesday, the environment was still stable, but suddenly someone staged a ridiculous drama of raising 96, rising by one yuan sharply, which was a sign of environmental change. The rest was stable. On Wednesday, Italy and Abyssinia had already started the war, but the long side was still stable. The first board fell more sharply, and the rest was slightly stable, similar to Tuesday. On Thursday, the situation was serious, and rumors arose at home and abroad, intensifying the downward trend. There were as many as seven types of stocks that broke the lowest price of November 11th of the previous month. On Friday, the Italy-Abyssinia war had begun, and Britain showed no signs of joining the vortex. Moreover, due to excessive declines in recent days, No. 48 covered short positions very aggressively, and market prices rebounded sharply, with a strong rebound. Gold short positions surged by 1.25 yuan, while selling pressure on No. 11 and No. 16 remained strong. On Saturday, the situation was slightly stable, and there was no new progress in the environment. Market prices were exhausted, and future changes were difficult to predict. International winds and clouds were still in a state of power struggle, hoping to reverse the situation, but it was feared that it would not be easy to change the people's minds. Last week's market price results showed a drop of 2-3 jiao to one yuan, with only 96 rising by about half a yuan. The total turnover was 95,381,000 yuan. Oil Market - The Crisis of White Tung Oil is Imminent

Since the price of white tung oil in Hanshi rose to 86 yuan per dan, most of the full-weight goods have been collected by various foreign firms, resulting in no market for several days. Currently, the goods handled by foreign firms are all underweight goods, and the prices vary. However, the combined full-weight price may be more than 86 yuan. However, because they need the goods, various foreign firms, although they dislike the high prices, still have to buy them. However, they are unwilling to do so, so various countries in Europe and the United States are widely planting tung trees domestically, hoping to increase production as soon as possible. And they are still not satisfied, reducing the tung oil content in the manufacture of paints in various paint factories. In the past, tung oil was mixed with other miscellaneous oils in equal proportions, but now only 30% tung oil is used. If so, the use of tung oil will be reduced a lot. Production increases while usage decreases, so that the tung oil needed in the future will not depend on foreign countries. It is heard that various countries have this plan. This kind of plan is all caused by the excessively high selling price in our country. Originally, if the price of tung oil was above 30 yuan per dan, it would be cost-effective for various countries in Europe and the United States to plant their own trees. Therefore, the selling price of tung oil in our country should not be too high. Today's price increase is actually inviting a crisis. Those who do not understand foreign trade think that they are selling at a good price and celebrate each other. In fact, high prices are feared. Now the market has reached its peak. Once there is a backlash, the day of a sharp decline is just around the corner.

Hongjiang Tung Oil Falls, Orders See Rise

Hongjiang tung oil has no export route and is only supplied to the domestic market, so the market's rise and fall is only one or two yuan at most, and it never rises as dramatically as white tung oil. However, it is fundamentally transformed by white tung oil. Now that raw materials have risen so much, even though it is the time of the autumn sales decline, it is still somewhat related to white tung oil, so people no longer underestimate it. This year's new goods will definitely have high costs, and the market will also see a big rise in prices. For example, Zheng Hong Jichang and He have sold orders for 34 yuan per barrel, and Fu Hong Yang Hengyuan Qing Yuanfeng have sold orders for 28 yuan. It seems that there is a possibility of further increases. However, because it is limited to domestic sales, even if it rises, it will be gradual.

Metals - American Tinplate Rises Endlessly

Whether it is 90-pound or 100-pound American tinplate, regardless of the pattern, the market rose sharply yesterday. The reason is that the bottom goods are extremely scarce and the fixed price is high, so people's minds are getting better. The estimated price is 2-3 yuan better than before. For example, 90-pound single-connection is opened at 17.5 yuan per box, and double-connection is opened at 34 yuan. 100-pound single-connection is opened at 18.5 yuan, and double-connection is opened at 37 yuan. It is found that apart from a small batch opened yesterday, there is still no large-scale business. According to the observation of the market's people, the market outlook is expected to rise again.

Free Talk

Cold Satire and Hot Scolding

- Jiang Jiping

There are now many people who do not like to read texts that scold people, saying that kind of thing cannot be considered literature. This is, of course, a prejudice. But in my opinion, the form of literature is not just one. Whether it is abuse, cold satire, hot ridicule, or humor, as long as it is a mature thing, it is definitely good. But it depends on whether your thinking is mature and whether the object of mockery is correct. Humor is also great if what is written can be like Cervantes' Don Quixote. Abuse depends on what you are scolding, and satire also depends on what you are satirizing. If, like Shaw, you satirize British customs and the ugliness of the aristocracy, laughing them to the point of being completely devastated, that is valuable. Like Turgenev, mocking the nobles who abused serfs with suggestive strokes is also valuable. He satirized those nobles who forced female slaves to sing and dance and drink all night, saying:

"If they showed some fatigue, he would hold his head with both hands and sigh, 'Ah! Poor, poor me! People are ignoring me...' Then the coachman would stimulate those women with a whip."

How profound is this mocking stroke. When we read "stimulate those women with a whip," we really don't feel like laughing, but we really can't laugh. There is a great sadness, a great sorrow of oppressed life, contained here. At the same time, on the other hand, it clearly exposes the vicious, hideous ugly face, and we really can't help but be angry. Our hearts are already filled with things that can burn, and this passage of his is like kindling. As soon as we read this article, the fire in our hearts will immediately burn. Isn't this kind of satirical thing good?

If it is said that the product of literature must have emotions, then the texts of cold satire and hot scolding are not without emotions. As in the example I mentioned above, Turgenev would not have been able to write such an article if he had not been extremely angry. From this passage, we can see that his emotions are extremely suppressed, but the more suppressed, the deeper the emotions, so it is written in this way. On the outside surface, it looks indifferent, but in fact, it contains deep emotions. Shaw's cold satire also seems to have gone through a period of anger. On the surface, it is laughable, but in fact, it is extremely thought-provoking, not like that simply a problem that is simply laughable. His articles have this kind of expression everywhere, and I will not give any more examples.

In terms of the style of writing, cold satire and hot scolding, it seems that cold satire is a little higher than hot scolding, but in fact, the two are the same. That is to say, in terms of human character, some people are calm and some people are enthusiastic. Calm people are not necessarily better than enthusiastic people. Kucagawa Bai Village has a piece about cold satire and hot scolding, and his opinion is very good. Let me copy it below:

"When it comes to mockery, at first you have to think of coldness, you have to think of the paleness of color. The so-called ridicule, the so-called satire, I think the colder it is, the more it will increase the taste of ridicule and pleasure. When it comes to scolding, at first you have to think of heat, and at the same time you have to associate it with angry hair, the hot blood and hot-tempered people with faces splashed with red. When the heat exceeds the boiling point, there you can see the pleasure of cursing, and the increase in the taste of enthusiasm. The former has a rational calmness, with plenty of leeway. And in its half, there is an unintentional accompaniment to a taste of disgust. The latter is from a heated emotional nature, so although it seems to have an unchanging naivety and straightforwardness, at the same time, I am afraid that it is inevitable that there will be a crazy and careless attitude. The former can be said to be like water like ice, and like a sharp blade, while the latter is like fire like flame, and like a sledgehammer. In the former, it can be seen as having a classical taste, and in the latter, there is a romantic interest."

This passage of his describing cold satire and hot scolding is exactly what I wanted to say but didn't say. In short, cold satire and hot scolding are equally important. This is the difference in the style of writing, not the height of character. Literature has tolerance, and the method of expression can be casual. Whether it is essays, dramas, or poems; humor, cold satire, hot scolding... it doesn't matter. The most important thing is only the word "consciousness". Is what you are mocking the public's hated? Is your target correct? If this purpose is correct, then this article is great and has permanent value.

We don't have to reject essays, and we don't have to specialize in worshiping novels. This is only a matter of form. There is also "consciousness" that is more important than form. Have we forgotten?

Guihua City

- Yuan Chenying

- One of the Impressions of Suiyuan -

The train crawled out of the railway lying across the Great Qingshan Mountain outside the Great Wall like a snake. It took a long breath. At the foot of the gloomy green pines of the Great Qingshan Mountain, the first thing that was revealed was the tall stone city wall of the new city two and a half miles south of the railway. After passing the city wall, you arrived at Suiyuan Station.

Jumping off the train, when you walk out of the station, if you are an outsider, the people selling snacks and drinks at the station will think: "Look! Today the masters and misses from Beijing are here for inspection again."

Walking down from the station. Sitting in a rickshaw pulled by a skinny hand. Slowly walking towards the city, passing over the stone-paved road. On both sides are tall poplar trees, and the leaves cast wide shadows. The road is quiet, and you will think: "What a quiet place!"

When the rickshaw reaches the place where the Catholic forces invaded this remote part of the Great Wall—the place where foreign adults do good deeds—the public hospital, the west city gate tower of the new city stands tall in the east, half-hidden and half-visible like a pagoda in a picture of a fairy scene. Two "人"-shaped roads to the southeast are laid out in front of you, and the rickshaw driver will turn his head and ask you: "Let's go to the old city?" When you nod, he will pull you weakly again, and stagger towards the south.

When you reach the south entrance of the road, it is exactly a four-mile-long east-west road from the old city to the new city, and the road to the station恰凑成a "丁"character. As soon as you turn the corner, you will see the big chimney of the Suiyuan Woolen Mill standing there, and the rumbling sound of the machine spreads in the air. Houses are being built on both sides of the road, and the road roller is like a clumsy cow, shaking its big belly, rolling back and forth on the road, and the pedestrians are walking past in twos and threes, quietly, like some mice, and the people riding bicycles are just like pulling a cow, slowly driving past.

When you are about to enter the old city, there is a very tall building, which was originally a memorial hall, but now it is going to be turned into a gathering place.

Walking into the city, the uneven road will make you feel breathless in the car. Under the poplar trees are rows of earthen houses. After passing this, you will enter Guihua City. The street is being rebuilt. The laborers who are打石子are constantly putting stones on the road. The stones are flying up and flying towards your body, which will suddenly scare you.

Although the Public Security Bureau reported that the number of stores paying business tax has decreased from 7,000 to 3,000, the stores on the North Gate Street are being knocked down and rebuilt one by one, widened and rebuilt! The road is narrow! How can cars pass through? So, the road is wider, so...

On the two-mile-long South Street, all kinds of people are crowded at the street head. Lamas wearing clumsy cassocks, Hui people wearing university doctorate hats, and most of them are Han people. People are crowded like ants at the crossroads. This place should also be widened! However—however...

The store's gramophone is playing various musics,嘩拉嘩拉的, and the sound of cars and rickshaws奏出了this desert city's symphony. When night covers the land outside the Great Wall, there are many people standing under the flashing electric lights listening to the radio, but the owner of the store is sighing! "Just listen! Things can't be sold! Ah! Why are the villagers (Note 1) so poor?…" Slowly, he also has to immerse himself in the 嘩拉嘩拉的 evening radio music with those listeners.

(Note 1) "Villager" is the word for farmer outside the Great Wall.

The Story of a Horse (Part 1)

— Lin Shi

This horse, because it was covered in a deep chestnut coat, was given a beautiful name by its master. It has had this beautiful name for several years, and as a result, it has lived in its master's house for many years as well.

It is not wrong to say that it is truly quite foolish. When it was young, it didn't need to wait for the master's whip to lash its backside; it could run thirty or forty *li* (Chinese miles) in one go without resting. The master would ride it everywhere to collect rent, and also ride it to go hunting, and sometimes even have it pull the carriage for the ladies. He would almost always praise it for being truly able to run. And when it heard these words of praise, it would screech in a high-pitched voice and let out a long cry, expressing the indescribable joy in its heart.

Not only could it run, but it could also eat. In spring and summer, needless to say, the fields were full of lush grass that filled its big belly. In winter, when its master occasionally gave it a few *sheng* (a unit of dry measure) of grain in addition to the chopped dry rice straw, it would also happily cry out.

But the era of youth and strength has long since passed. It had a full set of teeth until two years ago. Now this horse is old.

Today, from morning until now, it is still gnawing on that bucket of dry rice straw. It has not tasted grain for quite some time. The rice straw is so dry and hard, it feels like chewing on many iron nails, causing pain all over its mouth. It thinks that it would be good if only the master would scald the rice straw with boiling water, but even this cannot be fulfilled.

While slowly chewing on the straw, it surveys its surroundings. The sun has already climbed very high. Thin white clouds float in the sky. The branches of the trees in the garden have sprouted green buds and new leaves at some point. It seems that winter has quietly passed, and the fragrant breath of spring has once again spread across the human world.

After a long time, it finally fills its belly. The warm sun shines on its body, making it feel pleasantly warm. It shivers all over, and a lot of the shed winter fur scatters on the ground. It seems to be stimulated by the sun and feels very energetic. It hasn't cried out for a long time, so it thinks about it and lets out a loud cry, crying very enthusiastically and for a long time. But the master, hearing its cry from inside the house, walks to the corridor and smiles and scolds it from afar:

"Ha! You old beast, you're finally crying out!"

As the master says these words, the tall gray dog beside him also barks twice along with the master.

"Old beast!" The master has often used this phrase to scold it in recent years. Before, he would happily call it by its name, but now he starts every sentence with "old beast." Thinking about this, it cannot help but feel resentful and unhappy. However, it also knows very well that it is indeed old. But it also thinks: That mongrel dog also barked at me twice along with the master? Does it deserve to? Ha! Lowly beast! Dogs are much more lowly than horses.

Soon, the master brings out the saddle and bridle, saying:

"Old beast, I'm taking you hunting today." Then he straps the saddle on its back, and the bit in the bridle tightly binds its mouth. It has had many experiences with hunting; in the mountains and forests, it would gallop very fast with the master on its back. The master would aim his gun at wild animals like roe deer and rabbits, and the living creatures would fall to the ground, dripping with bright red blood.

Now it is going hunting again. Sure enough, the master is wearing light and agile short clothes and carrying a gun. The leather whip sways in front of its eyes a few times, and then he straddles its back. Suddenly, a hundred or so *jin* (about 110 pounds) of weight is added to its body, and its legs cannot help but weaken a little. The morning sun has made it feel lazy, and it really doesn't want to run, but when it thinks about the stinging pain of the leather whip, it has no choice but to run forward.

Husband and Wife Over Firewood and Rice

Dusk at Silver Terrace Mountain

— Ding Di

Taking advantage of the evening glow, I climbed Silver Terrace Mountain, now renamed Boxian Park. The late summer breeze was already carrying a slight coolness as it brushed against our bodies. The night slowly descended. The rows of willows planted recently by Boxian abruptly darkened.

Looking up at the sky, the blue turned gray. One bird, then another, then another, I counted to myself. Walking to the top of the mountain, the houses were arranged like pigeons' or bees' nests below. In the distance, one light, two lights, vague and lonely little nocturnes!

The wind blew harder and harder. Immediately, my heart also floated up. At first, there were waves of fantastical floating thoughts, and then even the floating thoughts disappeared. My heart was as serene as the wind in March. The Buddhist concept of no ego and no attachment to anything, perhaps that's what it's like?

The wind blew my clothes up, rustling. Even my heart and lungs felt thoroughly clear. I shifted my gaze to the very far, very far distance: I vaguely saw the ancient Wucheng (Wuhu) and the moon over Guazhou (near Nanjing). Ultimately, was I forgetting my emotions about things, or were things forgetting their emotions about me? I was lost.

At the height of my bewilderment, a kind of primal, confused, excited, and happy emotion that primitive humans often had arose. I jumped, I wildly waved my hands. The people who came with me all laughed.

We turned right from Boxian Temple. There was a slanting dirt slope going down, about several *zhang* (approximately 10 feet). At the end of the road, it was impossible to go up any further. There were only overgrown thorns and mounds of earth and rocks. Step by step we walked downwards, and a smear of rouge-colored sunset was at the same level as us. Beautiful sunset! How should I praise it?

Below the mountain, there was a stretch of paddy fields submerged in water. At first glance, it seemed impossible to recognize those as the cloud-like fields that produced rice and wheat. Now, part of them was in the water, and part was on land. Half of the nearby houses were also submerged in water. When I saw those, I immediately thought of a series of images of refugees from the flood.

The flying birds returned to the forest, the cicadas had stopped singing, and the twilight gradually deepened.

Approaching the corridor of Boxian Temple, I saw the magnificent architecture steeped in the desolate atmosphere of this dusk. A feeling of nostalgia mixed with the sigh that "The great river flows eastward, sweeping away countless historical figures" filled me. In addition to mourning Mr. Boxian, I also mourned this enigmatic life.

There were more electric lights than when we came. Each one was embedded on the curtain of the black universe. I stepped on Silver Terrace's famous "Evening Glow" and walked to the park's teahouse.

The Honorary Old Woman (Part 3)

— Written by Ema Shū, Translated by Ren Jun

On the way home, I told her about the things that I had suddenly thought of during the war. The mobilization notices, the send-offs for the soldiers going to war, the news and special editions announcing the war and victories, the lives of the fallen acquaintances and their bereaved families... everywhere, there were only the two words "honorary." Everywhere was honorary. Honorary soldiers, honorary victories, honorary deaths...

Then, I thought of that long-forgotten honorary old woman. Yes, there once was a person called the honorary old woman. Even so, in reality, for a long time, I seemed to have completely forgotten her, and had not thought of her at all.

Therefore, I could not help but tell my wife the story of this strange old woman.

The so-called honorary old woman was, no, was a nickname. And it was a nickname that people had unconsciously given her during the war. Her real name was Cooking Old Woman, and she was the cook in my house.

When did the Cooking Old Woman first come to my house? Regarding this, I have no exact memory. I'm afraid she came a long time ago, perhaps when I was still a child. Her hair was always disheveled and messy, she had deeply sunken and strangely gleaming eyes, a toothless mouth that only revealed red gums when she smiled, a sallow complexion, and she was dressed sloppily without any regard. No matter how people looked at her, they would feel that she was not an ordinary old woman. In fact, we often thought of her as crazy. Of course, she didn't say or do anything particularly strange, but one could always see things that felt a little peculiar. Therefore, she never seemed to be suitable to be the cook, who should be clean. However, she was indeed a very hardworking woman, not lazy at all. She single-handedly took care of almost all the cooking for the hundred female workers in the silk mill and many other servants. Therefore, my mother liked her very much. Everyone else also had good feelings toward her.

She had a small, impoverished home on the edge of the market. There were also a husband and an only son named Yongzao. When the old woman talked about Yongzao, those strangely gleaming eyes would take on an indescribable tenderness, and a seemingly proud glow would appear on her sallow face. Especially when he was deemed fit for Category A service during the conscription examination, the old woman was even more proud. Her son was selected to be a soldier for the country! She seemed to feel that this was simply the supreme glory for a poor family. Moreover, before this joy and pride, she seemed to have completely forgotten that when the oarsman was taken into the army, the family's life would immediately become difficult.
